</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Statins" title="Statins">Statins</a> are effective in preventing further cardiovascular disease in people with a history of cardiovascular disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statins20122_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-Statins20122-157">[157]</a></sup> As the event rate is higher in men than in women, the decrease in events is more easily seen in men than women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Statins20122_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-Statins20122-157">[157]</a></sup> In those at risk, but without a history of cardiovascular disease (primary prevention), statins decrease the risk of death and combined fatal and non-fatal cardiovascular disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> The benefit, however, is small.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> A United States guideline recommends statins in those who have a 12% or greater risk of cardiovascular disease over the next ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Niacin_(nutrient)" title="Niacin (nutrient)">Niacin</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fibrates" title="Fibrates">fibrates</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CETP_Inhibitors" title="CETP Inhibitors">CETP Inhibitors</a>, while they may increase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HDL_cholesterol" title="HDL cholesterol">HDL cholesterol</a> do not affect the risk of cardiovascular disease in those who are already on statins.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> Fibrates lower the risk of cardiovascular and coronary events, but there is no evidence to suggest that they reduce all-cause mortality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-diabetic_medication" title="Anti-diabetic medication">Anti-diabetic medication</a> may reduce cardiovascular risk in people with Type 2 diabetes, although evidence is not conclusive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> A meta-analysis in 2009 including 27,049 participants and 2,370 major vascular events showed a 15% <a href="/wiki/Relative_risk_reduction" title="Relative risk reduction">relative risk reduction</a> in cardiovascular disease with more-intensive glucose lowering over an average follow-up period of 4.4 years, but an increased risk of major <a href="/wiki/Hypoglycemia" title="Hypoglycemia">hypoglycemia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Aspirin" title="Aspirin">Aspirin</a> has been found to be of only modest benefit in those at low risk of heart disease, as the risk of serious bleeding is almost equal to the protection against cardiovascular problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> In those at very low risk, including those over the age of 70, it is not recommended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Preventive_Services_Task_Force" title="United States Preventive Services Task Force">United States Preventive Services Task Force</a> recommends against use of aspirin for prevention in women less than 55 and men less than 45 years old; however, it is recommended for some older people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup>
</p><p>The use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vasoactive" title="Vasoactive">vasoactive</a> agents for people with pulmonary hypertension with left heart disease or hypoxemic lung diseases may cause harm and unnecessary expense.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ACCPandATSfive2_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-ACCPandATSfive2-169">[169]</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Antibiotics for secondary prevention of coronary heart disease</b>
</p><p>Antibiotics may help patients with coronary disease to reduce the risk of heart attacks and strokes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-170">[170]</a></sup> However, evidence in 2021 suggests that antibiotics for secondary prevention of coronary heart disease are harmful, with increased mortality and occurrence of stroke;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_170-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-170">[170]</a></sup> the use of antibiotics is not supported for preventing secondary coronary heart disease.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_activity">Physical activity</span></h3>
<p>Exercise-based cardiac rehabilitation following a heart attack reduces the risk of death from cardiovascular disease and leads to less hospitalizations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndersonThompson2021_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-AndersonThompson2021-171">[171]</a></sup> There have been few high-quality studies of the benefits of exercise training in people with increased cardiovascular risk but no history of cardiovascular disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>A systematic review estimated that inactivity is responsible for 6% of the burden of disease from coronary heart disease worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> The authors estimated that 121,000 deaths from coronary heart disease could have been averted in Europe in 2008 if people had not been physically inactive. Low-quality evidence from a limited number of studies suggest that yoga has beneficial effects on blood pressure and cholesterol.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Tentative evidence suggests that home-based exercise programs may be more efficient at improving exercise adherence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dietary_supplements">Dietary supplements</span></h3>
<p>While a <a href="/wiki/Healthy_diet" title="Healthy diet">healthy diet</a> is beneficial, the effect of <a href="/wiki/Antioxidant" title="Antioxidant">antioxidant</a> supplementation (<a href="/wiki/Vitamin_E" title="Vitamin E">vitamin E</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C">vitamin C</a>, etc.) or vitamins has not been shown to protect against cardiovascular disease and in some cases may possibly result in harm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> Mineral supplements have also not been found to be useful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Niacin_(nutrient)" title="Niacin (nutrient)">Niacin</a>, a type of vitamin B3, may be an exception with a modest decrease in the risk of cardiovascular events in those at high risk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Magnesium" title="Magnesium">Magnesium</a> supplementation lowers high blood pressure in a dose-dependent manner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jee2002_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jee2002-183">[183]</a></sup> Magnesium therapy is recommended for people with ventricular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart_arrhythmia" title="Heart arrhythmia">arrhythmia</a> associated with <a href="/wiki/Torsades_de_pointes" title="Torsades de pointes">torsades de pointes</a> who present with <a href="/wiki/Long_QT_syndrome" title="Long QT syndrome">long QT syndrome</a>, and for the treatment of people with digoxin intoxication-induced arrhythmias.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zipes2006_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zipes2006-184">[184]</a></sup> There is no evidence that <a href="/wiki/Omega-3_fatty_acid" title="Omega-3 fatty acid">omega-3 fatty acid</a> supplementation is beneficial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span></h2>
<p>Cardiovascular disease is treatable with initial treatment primarily focused on diet and lifestyle interventions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_3-29"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Influenza" title="Influenza">Influenza</a> may make heart attacks and strokes more likely and therefore <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Influenza_vaccination" title="Influenza vaccination">influenza vaccination</a> may decrease the chance of cardiovascular events and death in people with heart disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p><p>Proper CVD management necessitates a focus on MI and stroke cases due to their combined high mortality rate, keeping in mind the cost-effectiveness of any intervention, especially in developing countries with low or middle-income levels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_89-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-89">[89]</a></sup> Regarding MI, strategies using aspirin, atenolol, streptokinase or tissue plasminogen activator have been compared for quality-adjusted life-year (QALY) in regions of low and middle income. The costs for a single QALY for aspirin and atenolol were less than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US$" title="US$">US$</a>25, streptokinase was about $680, and t-PA was $16,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zip2018_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Zip2018-187">[187]</a></sup> Aspirin, ACE inhibitors, beta-blockers, and statins used together for secondary CVD prevention in the same regions showed single QALY costs of $350.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Zip2018_187-1"><a href="#cite_note-Zip2018-187">[187]</a></sup>
</p><p>There are also surgical or procedural interventions that can save someone's life or prolong it. For heart valve problems, a person could have surgery to replace the valve. For arrhythmias, a <a href="/wiki/Artificial_cardiac_pacemaker" title="Artificial cardiac pacemaker">pacemaker</a> can be put in place to help reduce abnormal heart rhythms and for a heart attack, there are multiple options two of these are a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coronary_angioplasty" title="Coronary angioplasty">coronary angioplasty</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Coronary_artery_bypass_surgery" title="Coronary artery bypass surgery">coronary artery bypass surgery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>There is probably no additional benefit in terms of mortality and serious adverse events when blood pressure targets were lowered to ≤ 135/85 mmHg from ≤ 140 to 160/90 to 100 mmHg.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Epidemiology">Epidemiology</span></h2>

color:black;"> </span> 1,450–1,802</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff9a20; color:white;"> </span> 5,272–10233</div></div></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="940" decoding="async" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/290px-Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/435px-Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg/580px-Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg.png 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cardiovascular_diseases_world_map_-_DALY_-_WHO2004.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Disability-adjusted life year for cardiovascular diseases per 100,000 inhabitants in 2004<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Health_Organization_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-World_Health_Organization-16">[16]</a></sup><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1054258005" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="refbegin refbegin-columns references-column-count references-column-count-2" style="column-count: 2;"> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#b3b3b3; color:black;"> </span> no data</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffff65; color:black;"> </span> &lt;900</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#fff200; color:black;"> </span> 900–1650</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffdc00; color:black;"> </span> 1650–2300</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffc600; color:black;"> </span> 2300–3000</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ffb000; color:black;"> </span> 3000–3700</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff9a00; color:black;"> </span> 3700–4400</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff8400; color:black;"> </span> 4400–5100</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff6e00; color:black;"> </span> 5100–5800</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff5800; color:black;"> </span> 5800–6500</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff4200; color:black;"> </span> 6500–7200</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ff2c00; color:black;"> </span> 7200–7900</div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#cb0000; color:white;"> </span> &gt;7900</div> </div></div></div></div>
<p>Cardiovascular diseases are the leading cause of death worldwide and in all regions except Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WHO2011_3-30"><a href="#cite_note-WHO2011-3">[3]</a></sup> In 2008, 30% of all global death was attributed to cardiovascular diseases. Death caused by cardiovascular diseases are also higher in low- and middle-income countries as over 80% of all global deaths caused by cardiovascular diseases occurred in those countries. It is also estimated that by 2030, over 23 million people will die from cardiovascular diseases each year.
</p><p>It is estimated that 60% of the world's cardiovascular disease burden will occur in the South Asian subcontinent despite only accounting for 20% of the world's population. This may be secondary to a combination of genetic predisposition and environmental factors. Organizations such as the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Heart_Association" title="Indian Heart Association">Indian Heart Association</a> are working with the <a href="/wiki/World_Heart_Federation" title="World Heart Federation">World Heart Federation</a> to raise awareness about this issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Indian_Heart_190-0"><a href="#cite_note-Indian_Heart-190">[190]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heart-on-a-chip" title="Heart-on-a-chip">Heart-on-a-chip</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vessel-on-a-chip" title="Vessel-on-a-chip">Vessel-on-a-chip</a></div>
<p>There is evidence that cardiovascular disease existed in pre-history,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> and research into cardiovascular disease dates from at least the 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup>  The causes, prevention, and/or treatment of all forms of cardiovascular disease remain active fields of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biomedical_research" title="Biomedical research">biomedical research</a>, with hundreds of scientific studies being published on a weekly basis.
</p><p>Recent areas of research include the link between inflammation and atherosclerosis<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup>  the potential for novel therapeutic interventions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> and the genetics of coronary heart disease.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

ins%2C+H&amp;rft.au=Kathiresan%2C+S&amp;rft.au=McPherson%2C+R&amp;rft.au=Deloukas%2C+P&amp;rft.au=Schunkert%2C+H&amp;rft.au=Samani%2C+NJ&amp;rft.au=Farrall%2C+M&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fdiscovery.dundee.ac.uk%2Fws%2Ffiles%2F7268983%2FCAD1000G2015.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACardiovascular+disease"></span></span>
